B0025KVLTC|5.0|I just bought the Beatles Revolver (UK version) cd on amazon.  And I have listened to it a couple times in my car and just love it.  The UK version from 1966 has 3 additional songs that I have never heard before- I'm Only Sleeping, And Your Bird Can Sing, and Dr. Robert.  So, its like hearing brand new Beatles songs.  Which is great.  Revolver is considered by many Beatles fans to be their best album, although most \\"best ofs\\" list Sgt Peppers as the greatest rock n roll album of all-time.  What I would say is that Revolver is a real ground-breaking kind of album.  The best songs are Taxman, Eleanor Rigby, and Tomorrow Never Knows- the 1st, 2nd and last tracks.  Harrison, McCartney, and Lennon respectively.  I've read Taxman is punk/soul 10 years before punk was created.  Eleanor Rigby was the first \\"rock song\\" to have a string quartet and probably the first to not have any bass, guitar, drum, or keyboard.  John Lennon invented psychedelic music (I think) with Tomorrow Never Knows - my favorite.  One guitar chord, a five beat drum riff, humming sitar and a lot of weird sounds.  And Lennon singing like a rock god.  You don't even need the mind-altering substances to appreciate the musical trip.  Listening to Dr. Robert I thought to myself this doesn't really sound like Beatles, it almost sounds like early Jefferson Airplane.  Then  I read a review of She Said She Said from one of my many Beatle books and it said Revolver started the West Coast or the San Francisco rock sound- the Airplane, Dead, Big Brother, etc.  Never heard that before.  Harrison has a song Love You To that I believe is the first sitar Indian rock song.  I was thinking I don't think anyone followed up on \\"Indian\\" rock, although Jimmy Page's Black Mountain Side and White Summer sound a lot like Harrison's guitar on this one.  My favorite McCartney song on the album- Got to Get You Into My Life, again doesn't sound like Beatles- has a r&b horn section- they had never done that before and sounds like Otis Redding or the Blues Brothers.  Then it has Ringo's Yellow Submarine which some say is how young children were introduced to the Beatles.  Ironic since Ringo later went onto be the voice for Thomas the Tank Engine.  Finally, I'm Only Sleeping has the first backward guitar solo- which the Beatles discovered by accident playing a tape the wrong way and went with it.  It is said that all psychedelic music from that point on had to have backward guitars and other effects.      So, i just keep playing the album and loving it!

After all, \\"the estate\\" is also comprised of family, and if they truly didn't believe it was Michael singing Breaking News, then it would not be on the CD. The Jacksons aren't just music royalty, they're American icons. Beyond that, they know how to create buzz; they've been doing it for decades, and arguably doing it better than anyone. They even hired two teams of audio forensic analysts to verify the recording's authenticity; it's 100% MJ, and 100% Sizzle!<br /><br />\\"Hold My Hand\\" was released next, and the sizzle there was that it was an over-produced Akon song with just a smattering of MJ looped to fill out a sparse vocal track. Well, I'm no music producer, or self-proclaimed audio expert timing clips and counting the loops of MJ's vocals -- and with all due respect to the detractors, it all sounds a bit like spinning a Beatles record backwards looking for the hidden message. I'm just content to be an average listener, and on that basis, I have to say I truly love Hold My Hand. No, it isn't Heal The World, or Earth Song, but it IS classic Michael -- a simple yet universal tune that everyone on the planet can relate to, no matter the age, country or period in time. Everyone, young and old, lovers or friends, parents or children -- knows the simple comfort and love that comes with holding someone's hand -- classic MJ through and through. And some of the most memorable songs in history are the simplest with sparse writing and musicianship; and this song is much more than that. It's hip, cool, current and catchy. L-O-V-E it! This could easily be Michael's next #1 hit! And the music video is stunning, heartwarming and bittersweet. To see the way they used archival footage of Michael (some we haven't even seen before) the different races, age groups, and even the disabled -- the visuals ooze Michael through and through; it's clear they had his spirit, memory and intentions in mind. Bravo! Brilliant! A stunning tribute to the late King, and a befitting first video to emerge from his posthumous work.<br /><br />The next song to be previewed was \\"Much Too Soon,\\" an aptly titled ditty since MJ left the world and us all much too soon. Like Hold My Hand, the tune is simple and gentle, yet sweet. I consider it to be MJ unplugged - sparse and delicate music, accompanied by Michael's angelic vocals. I think that's what always impressed me most about Michael's vocals -- his ability to rock our world with Bad or Earth Song, and then a gentle tune like this, with such pure and effortless mastery. Unlike the other pre-released tracks, there was no controversy about if this was really MJ singing, or that his vocals were too sparse. Actually, it was very well received and is a hauntingly beautiful track -- again, classic MJ. The man had a knack for making simple, yet universal tunes that are relatable to the masses, which isn't easy to pull off. Remember, this is the guy who made us cry when he sang about his pet mouse! And we all related that to our own relationships and lives -- simply masterful, and at such a young age! But then, MJ himself said it best, \\"I was a veteran before I was a teenager.\\"<br /><br />Next, a snippet of Hollywood Tonight premiered on the Ellen show, but not enough to really appreciate it. But after hearing the full track, I just love the beat. The song starts with what sounds like a church choir, followed by MJ beat-boxing and free styling vocally before the song reaches full lift-off. Cool song, great beat, high energy and gets you moving in your seat -- or in my case, impulsively jutting my head and shoulders in a lame MJ impersonation. The tune has an interestingly haunting feel, especially near the end. Cool!<br /><br />I Can't Make It Another Day with Lenny Kravitz was the next preview to debut, and the instant I heard the beat, I could just picture MJ grooving and wowing us with his legendary moves. This one feels the most like MJ at his best, and is the most authentic song on the entire CD; like it was plucked right off one of his best selling albums. I don't know what album this got cut from, but it completely holds its own and is on par with his previous works. This song could easily go #1, if handled right. And unlike Hold My Hand, it's not actually a duet. Lenny makes a fantastic musical contribution (I've always thought he is cool and talented) and backs up the King vocally, while the rest is all MJ in full vocal spectrum and power like only he can pull off. What a great song! Sounds like classic Michael from the 80's but apparently was recorded in 2008! I keep listening to it over and over -- Love this one! Go MJ! In other words: \\"Yo Dawg, it's hot, Hot, HOT!\\"<br /><br />Next, there were some very brief audio clips played on Oprah, but that's the basic breakdown of how the previews were rolled out. As for the rest of the CD...<br /><br />One can't help but wonder what Michael would have thought of all this. Or how he would have changed all these tunes had he known they were going to be released. Clearly he didn't see a place for them prior or we would have heard them all before now. But even though these are \\"B\\" tracks that MJ didn't really approve of on some level, they are still sung by the King of Pop and carry with them, all his talent and excellence. \\"This Is It\\" was just raw rehearsal footage, yet remained mesmerizing thanks to the man who was its focal point. Having said that, there's definitely songs here that rise above the rest, while others are a little lacking for me; here's my breakdown:<br /><br />Keep Your Head Up - is a passionate, optimistic song. That's MJ for ya, trying to give us hope and something to believe in. This one can't help but make one feel there's a light at the end of the tunnel (and that it's not an oncoming train!) It's nowhere near the level of Man In The Mirror or Will You Be There, or even Cry, but it's definitely of that ilk. I love it!<br /><br />(I Like) The Way You Love Me - is pure bubble-gum pop; no stellar vocals or hook, and not all that memorable. The best part of the song is the opening, which has a brief clip of MJ leaving a voice mail or speaking on the phone to someone and explaining how he envisions the song -- great insight! I'm not all that fond of the mix, but it's still an ok song. I think a little less going on musically would have made MJ's vocals shine through better. An acoustic version maybe, with less of the airy 70's hot air balloon and rainbows type feel. But then, maybe that's just how MJ wanted it.<br /><br />Monster - featuring 50 cent, has a lot of power behind it with a good hook. I'm not usually a 50 cent fan, but I like it. For me, it's not on the level of other great tracks on this CD (like Hold Your Hand or I Can't Make It Another Day) but it's kinda catchy and has a good feel to it. It's in the same ilk as Jam, but not as good. However, I do find myself moving to the beat and enjoying it; a solid entry within the context of this CD.<br /><br />Best Of Joy - a decent tune, but another one that's reminiscent of a 70's kind of mix. I know it wasn't recorded in that era, its just the impression I got. A bit dated in feel, and a middle of the road track compared to the rest of this CD, but still decent enough. Though it certainly doesn't hold up against MJ's top hits and most famous songs.<br /><br />Behind The Mask - WOW! What an amazing song; definitely one of the best on the entire CD! It has a great opening, a great beat, and the usual high energy vocals we love and expect from MJ. My foot just started tapping all on its own on this one, and I was grooving with MJ before I even realized my body was bopping to the beat. It was just innate and natural; classic MJ, infusing his music and passion into us via osmosis. It's songs like this that make it hard to believe he's really gone -- lively, upbeat and downright infectious. It's vocals like this that made him King. A really great song with a good shot at being a K.O. hit for the K.O.P. -- Hee-Hee! -- Glove to Michael!<br /><br />Lastly, a few words about the CD cover art itself -- just like the Hold My Hand video, this is the first posthumous cover, and as such, it has a lot to live up to; our memory of Michael, honoring his legacy, the invariable criticism that follows him everywhere, even in death. But I think the art work is an impressive collage of MJ's life, career and most significant highlights. Apparently, there's a lot of Sony haters out there, and perhaps with good reason. But for me, I feel like they're making a good effort to put forth a CD his fans will love and appreciate; and the cover art is evidence of that. My sense is that they may not do all the right things at all times, but it seems like they'd like to honor MJ's memory and are as much his fans as the rest of us. It's cliche to blame the big bad money-grubbing corporation for all our frustrations, and there may very well be some questionable things going on behind the scenes. But overall, I do sense an immense love and admiration behind what they're doing for MJ. It's just a little too cynical to blame it all on the greed of making money. A whole team of people are helping to put these projects forth, and they won't enjoy much success (or profits) if their intentions are solely cynical and tainted. I bet most of the people working behind the scenes love MJ as much as the rest of us, and are likely very proud to be part of these new projects and feel a heavy responsibility to do right by MJ, his family, his children and his fans. And speaking of which, MJ's family is involved in all this to some degree too, so that adds to the love behind all this that I'm sensing.<br /><br />A humble word to the detractors -- many people are convinced this CD is a fake, and that it's not really MJ singing. Just like there were many convinced that MJ couldn't handle the 50 dates in London -- but what are those people really saying? -- That Michael was a has-been, that he was completely washed up? That his talent no longer shined as bright? That he lost his voice, his electricity, his genius? That he was so delusional and intellectually vapid that he didn't know his own limits? Surely you couldn't mean that; not if you ever truly loved him and his talents. MJ was a perfectionist and would never have agreed to take the O2 stage if he didn't believe he could handle it; and was likely very proud of his Guinness Record for selling out 50 shows. And as far as this not being MJ singing on this CD -- are those same detractors saying MJ's talents are so ordinary that they are easily replicated by a common impersonator? And WHO is this impersonator, and if they have the talent to flawlessly impersonate the King, WHY don't they have a stratospheric career all their own? American Idol has probably auditioned a million singers over the span of all its seasons -- have they found any Michael Jacksons? Talent like that is extremely rare -- once in a lifetime rare. So I just don't buy the whole impersonator thing. MJ's talents are legendary and can't be duped by anyone. However, to those MJ detractors, I say -- more power to you! Keep those conspiracy theories alive, because it all adds to Michael's sizzle. Because in show business, you're truly dead and forgotten when everyone stops talking about you.<br /><br />Bottom Line -- At first listen, I thought this CD didn't measure up within the context of Michael's entire catalog, shoulder to shoulder against greats like Thriller, Bad, Dangerous, Off The Wall, etc. But after repeated listenings, I have to say this CD is pretty stellar. I'm giving it 5 stars -- because although these are tracks MJ never intended to release, like This Is It, they offer a rare behind the scenes glimpse into the creative process of the greatest and most successful entertainer in history. And that unique aspect alone makes these songs all the more priceless. For me, this isn't about finding a lost hit to rival Thriller, or finding a new Billie Jean; nor do I think that's realistic. It's about peeking behind the curtain to see how the wizard worked, and embracing this talented, unique icon in ways he would never have allowed were he alive. Having said that, songs like Behind The Mask, I Can't Make It Another Day, Hold My Hand and Much Too Soon WILL be timeless, memorable new hits for MJ and will be standouts from his entire catalog not only for their musicianship, but because they are posthumous masterpieces. And incidentally -- if Michael were alive to support this CD with his genius moves, a This Is It world tour, and the invariable media frenzy that would follow -- I'm confident many of these songs would skyrocket out of the stratosphere; a place MJ was quite at home and has always resided.<br /><br />In some ways, Michael's self-created \\"sizzle\\" was designed to keep us all at bay, and only now, in hindsight, are we able to get the intimate look into his life and creative process that we've always craved. No, the MJ of this world would not have liked that; but if he continues to exist in the great beyond, I bet he's quite happy with all of this. Obviously, Michael would have done things differently with all this music were he alive to oversee their mastering; likely he would have kept most of them unreleased. But even MJ's \\"B-side\\" rejects are impressive and better than most artists out there.<br /><br />Much has been said about Sony \\"botching\\" the release of this much anticipated CD, but personally, I think they've done a great job. Face it, you can't please everyone. Especially with someone like the late King of Pop; expectations and emotions are just too high. But they've been quite generous in giving us ample opportunity to hear all the songs in advance, and even tried to appease the King himself by making Hold My Hand the first official single;as MJ himself apparently wanted, via a handwritten note he left behind.<br /><br />Overall, this CD sounds very current and contemporary, and it's such a pleasure to have new music from a man we lost \\"Much Too Soon;\\" as per the aptly titled final track. Truth be told, I like this CD a whole lot. There will be those that won't be happy with anything posthumously released; for the rest of us, this is a great CD from a gem of a human being who continues to entertain and inspire -- a feat few ever accomplish while living, let alone from beyond the grave.<br /><br />Sometimes ya gotta stop griping about what woulda/coulda/shoulda been and be grateful for what we've got -- and what we just got from MJ is pretty darn great!<br /><br />Bravo, Michael... and thank you for continuing to give so generously.<br /><br />Keep Sizzling...being a K.O. hit for the K.O.P. -- Hee-Hee! -- Glove to Michael! 0316098337|5.0|Told through the voice of a five-year-old boy, \\"Room\\" feels disjointed and awkward at first. I almost gave up after five or six pages--and what a shame that would've been! By the twentieth page of Emma Donoghue's tale, I was in wonder, swept away into a world cramped and dark, but also full of love and hope. Ma has been trapped in a suburban garden shed for seven years, kidnapped by a lonely bachelor. Young Jack is the result of her kidnapper's unwanted attention, and yet Ma finds new reason to live through this beautiful, strong-willed child. It's a premise that sounds like something from the latest news flash, or from the reports of the Austrian man who held a woman in his basement for years.<br /><br />Jack is an unforgettable narrator, giving us glimpses into Room through his broken English. Though highly intelligent, he is sheltered beyond belief. Aside from the TV that is allowed by their kidnapper, Jack would have no insight into the Outside. Even so, he later says in his own words: \\"When I was four I didn't know about the world . . . Then Ma told me about if for real and I thought I knowed everything. But now I'm in the world all the time, I actually don't now much . . .\\" Jack and Ma begin to imagine a way of escape, and the results of their attempt are surprising, inevitable, incredible, and entirely believable. Donoghue has created a masterpiece, entering the psyche of a sheltered boy and revealing his hopes and fears with marvelous literary and imaginative skills. Over and over, I was amazed at the authenticity in Jack's responses to the world around him. Ma, too, responds to her shifting world in ways that are tragic, courageous, and humble. In the end, together, their responses lead to a poignant and understated conclusion.<br /><br />Through the course of the story, we see that Jack enjoys making word salads, combining two words to form new ones. He knows he must be brave even when he's scared: he must be \\"scave.\\" And, when he runs into a situation that is cool but also scary, he calls it \\"coolary.\\" It's a fine description of this novel, cool, scary, dark, and full of light. In \\"Room,\\" my favorite novel of 2010, Emma Donoghue has created a work similar to a Van Gogh--crude, yet vibrant and colorful; childlike, yet unmistakably genius.so scary, he calls it \\"coolary.\\" It's a fine description of this novel, cool, scary, dark, and full of light. B000HEWEJO|5.0|What more can be said about \\"It's A Wonderful Life,\\" consistently ranked among the world's greatest films? It's funny, and gripping, and suspenseful, and gut-wrenching, and the final scene makes you want to stand up and cheer, with happy tears running down your cheeks.<br /><br /> George Bailey is a quintessential American in this most American of films: From childhood, this bright, energetic youth wants to \\"shake the dust of this crummy little town\\" Bedford Falls from his feet, see the world, build things, do great deeds. But ... while his mind wants to do things for himself, his spirit instinctively and unhesitatingly drives him to help others. He saves his younger brother from drowning, losing the hearing in one ear in the process; he saves his part-time employer the druggist Mr. Gower from accidentally poisoning a family with a prescription wrongly mixed while Gower is mourning the death of his son. Later, as an adult, George Bailey saves his late father's savings and loan from the clutches of the grasping millionaire Henry F. Potter, the \\"meanest man in town\\" who puts us greatly in mind of Ebenezer Scrooge.<br /><br /> George marries his childhood sweetheart, Mary Hatch. The scene I remember the most clearly from the first time I saw the film, as a child, was the one where little Mary whispers into little George's left ear, which she believes he can't hear out of, \\"George Bailey, I'll love you 'til the day I die!\\" I've often wondered if he really didn't hear her -- or whether he just showed a remarkable self-possession for a young boy in not reacting.<br /><br /> Potter, thwarted in his efforts to destroy the Bailey Savings & Loan, finally calls George to his office one day and offers him \\"the chance of a lifetime\\" -- employment as Potter's properties manager, at an un-heard of (in 1946) $20,000 a year, trips to New York City and Europe for himself and his wife ... One thinks of Jesus Christ wandering in the desert, and Satan appearing and offering him all theriches in the world if he will only betray his mission on earth. George Bailey almost succumbs -- until he shakes hands with Potter, realizes what he's about to do, and with an angry wave of disgust, says, in effect, \\"Get thee behind me, Potter!\\"<br /><br /> The years pass, George and Mary have four children -- and then one day George's kind but bumbling uncle, Billy Bailey, loses $8,000 in cash of the savings and loan's money while on the way to deposit it in the bank. Events quickly spiral into the crucial night of George Bailey's life.<br /><br /> All is resolved happily in the denouement, of course; Americans have always demanded happy endings. This one is almost overwhelming, with all the people who have appeared in the film gathered in the Bailey living room on Christmas Eve, having come to the rescue of this unselfish, self-sacrificing man who has helped so many of them. As the camera pans all the by-now familiar faces, the crowd sings \\"Auld Lang Syne.\\" One is reminded of certain Shakespeare plays which also ended with a sing-along by the cast. Meanwhile, George, Mary and little Zuzu, their youngest child, decide that Clarence the Angel's saying, \\"Every time a bell rings, an angel gets his wings,\\" is true indeed.<br /><br /> The casting and direction of this movie are impeccable. It was the last and greatest of Frank Capra's series of \\"triumph of the little man\\" movies. James Stewart probably never gave a better performance; Donna Reed, not a towering star, was nevertheless just right as Mary Bailey. Lionel Barrymore's villain Potter is convincing to the nth degree. Thomas Mitchell, one of the great character actors, does a wonderful job as Uncle Billy, whose simple goodness is attested by the animals (the crow, the squirrel) who fly and scurry to him as to a close friend.<br /><br /> Is \\"It's A Wonderful Life\\" the best movie ever made? I don't know; most reviewers wouldn't rank it quite that high. But it's a wonderful film.
030746363X|5.0|From the moment my advanced copy arrived, I knew that Tim's latest book was a breakthrough read.  The 4-Hour Body is filled with information that will make an instant and positive difference in your relationship to your body.    Tim Ferriss is one of the unique authors who puts his words into practice and is able to show his readers exactly how to emulate his success. B00192IV9U|1.0|When I heard about the announcement in March of a new MJ album by Sony I was thrilled. Some fans said it was wrong of Sony to capitalize off of his unreleased material, but due to how nice the This Is It film was it seemed that a new album could only help his legacy. I would go on various fansites and the memebers were all anticipating this album for months. Finally in early November the album was finally announced. At first I thought it was kind of weird to have artwork of him in every era and call the CD \\"Michael\\" but then I thought I didn't care. I didn't want to be nitpicky and knew it was the music that mattered. After the announcement of the album some Jackson family members including his brothers, children, mother, and father all said that it is not his voice on the album. Me along with the rest of the fan community thought it was a made up story by the Jackson family who wanted to cause controversy like when Joe Jackson said that This Is It used body doubles, only to later withdraw that statement.     On November 8th the song Breaking News premiered online, I couldn't have been more excited. For the first minute or so of the song it was a funky instrumental beat and I was about to burst in anticipation of hearing the King of Pop's voice on this song. All of  the sudden I hear this strange voice saying \\"Everybody's talking the news of Michael Jackson\\". I thought that maybe there are other vocalists who take part in this song and was anticipating when Michael's voice would show up. I would occasional hear his screams which were blatantly sampled from older songs, and was waiting for his singing part in the song. I kept thinking that they picked such a terrible back up vocalist to duet with him and thought Mike's vocals could save the song. Before I knew it the song was over and Mike didnt sing at all besides a few grunts and mumbled words. Me, along with most of the fan community could not believe what had happened with this song, how could a company as big asSony publish a song like this under Michael's name? Well, it turns out that they were duped into not only buying 1, but 14 of these fake songs which were sold by Mike's friend Eddie Cascio and 3 are included on this album.    During the controversy some tabloid organizations who usually trash Michael started saying how great the song was and that his voice had just changed between recording 2001's Invincible and these 3 tracks in 2007. However, anyone who has seen the film This Is It knows how his voice sounded and although some playback was used, it was always apparent that Mike was singing vocals.     As made evident by Michael's nephew Taryll and brother Randy, the Eddie Cascio songs were copy righted just a few days after Michael died, and the Estate of Michael Jackson executors were so busy trying to start projects that they didn't even visit Mike's funeral. After the deal with Sony was made the executors visited the Cascio home, listened to the songs which were suspiciously only in finalized versions (no demo tapes, accapellas, or work tapes) and decided that the sounded enough like Mike and spent millions of dollars on the Cascio tracks. The reason Breaking News and the other Cascio songs have not been removed from the album are because the Michael Jackson Estate Executives who bought the songs do not want to lose their jobs due to negligence and that the upcoming holiday release of the album was imminent.    Ok now after the long back story I would like to break down the album track by track.    Hold My Hand- Demo leaked in 2008 online, was never a favorite of Jackson fans due to how cheesy it is but it seems like the perfect radio friendly song for fans of newer pop music. The mastering the have done to the demo and the inclusion of a new string arrangement along with additional MJ vocals that weren't in the internet demo made this song worthy of the Jackson name. 7/10    Hollywood Tonight- Supposedly recording in the 1999 Invincible sessions and additional vocals were added to it in 2007 by Michael, this song is another upbeat radio friendly dance track which is heavily designed to sound like newer pop artists. The vocals have obviously been autotoned, however it is unapparent if this was Jackson's intent or not. His nephew Taryll has a long speech during the bridge of the song that drags on just a bit too much but Mike's energy saves the song once the bridge is done. 8/10    Keep Your Head Up- The first Cascio track, style of the song is made to sound just like a song Michael would've written. The song is so cheesy and uninspired that it is laughable. Whoever the singer is sounds like some bad 90s boy band singer. This song is the biggest disgrace to Mike's legacy. 0/10    I Like The Way You Love Me- Sounds more polished than the version which was already released in 2004's The Ultimate Collection, has a nice intro which includes Mike beatboxing the rhythm over the phone. It's a great song but this should've been a bonus track for a deluxe version instead of a rerelease of the same song trying to say it's new material. 7/10    Monster (feat. 50 cent)- The most blatantly fake Michael Jackson song I have ever heard. The singer goes into a falsetto many times that sounds nothing like Michael. Its supposed to be a song about how the paparazzi are monsters, but Mike's days of constantly being stalked by tabloids were very light in 2007. Although I hate rap, at least 50 Cent's part is better than the song itself. Another song that tries too hard to sound like Michael Jackson, but so much so that it is an obvious fake. 0/10    Best of Joy- Probably the biggest gem of the whole album. A unique song that will make your heart stop from the first trace of his voice, it is this magic that only the real Micheal Jackson can have.  A ballad sung entirely in trademark falsetto where Jackson says \\"I am forever, We are forever\\", it sounds like a new style of song Jackson was creating that cannot be categorized. The song was recordeda few months before his death in summer 2009. So touching that it almost brought me to tears, and a great performance by Michael. 10/10    Breaking News- Already discussed in detail above, however I would like to say that having a song like this right after hearing Best Of Joy is disgusting and sucks away the magic Best of Joy created. 0/10    Another Day feat Lenny Kravitz- This song was put up online in January 2010, and is a great rock and roll song recorded during the 1999 Invincible sessions. The version here is a bit less powerful and hard edged than the version that was leaked online, however the vocals and instruments are cleaner. Knowing the soft type of album Invincible was, I believe that this is probably the way Michael intended the song to be. It is softer than the original but still rockin. 9/10    Behind The Mask- The vocals of this song were written and recorded by Michael after he heard the 1979 song of the same name by Japanese band Yellow Magic Orchestra. There were vocals he recorded in 81 for Thriller, which didnt make the cut and vocals recorded in 1985 for Bad which didn't fit in well with the rest of the album's tracks. His keyboardist Greg Philianges recorded and released version with him singing Michael's lyrics in 1984. This was the song I was anticipating most when \\"Michael's\\" tracklist was revealed. The song starts out with crowd noises and a jazzy saxophone, which really builds up energy for the rest of the track. The awesome Yellow Magic Orchestra instrumental kicks in with Mike beatboxing to it and his vocals are pure gold. The techno sounds are both futuristic sounding yet retro at the same time. Mike's voice is so high energy and this is probably my favorite song on the album. I believe Mike would be proud that this song was finally released. 10/10    Much Too Soon- A soft folk song which was recorded originally in 1987, then again recorded in 1994 to be released as an extra song on HIStory which was originally going to be a Greatest Hits album with just 1 or 2 new songs. The 1987 version has been online for a month, and what is released here in the 94 version. A touching song about love and rejection, and it is definitely a new style for Mike. However this really should have gone after a song like Best of Joy instead of the upbeat Behind the Mask. This is the perfect album closer though. 9/10    How is it that something that millions of fans around the world were wanting to buy was ruined so much that fans are keeping their money to not support what Sony has done to Michael. The album definitely has some great genuine Jackson songs, but since the rich stubborn Estate Executives have decided to keep the fake songs on, the whole project is a huge disrespect to Mike. I hope that fans realize what Sony and the Estate are trying to do with this, they are setting us up for an infinite supply of \\"lost MJ tracks\\" which are recorded by the Cascio track impersonator whenever Sony decides they need more money. The fact that there are dozens of real legitimate, great Michael Jackson songs from throughout his career on the internet such as Hot Street, Work That Body, Xscape, and Blue Gangster to name a few, makes it apparent that there are tons of great Michael Jackson outtakes from his 30 years as a solo artist. Don't buy this, don't let Sony fool you into giving them money for fake tracks, by not purchasing this you are encouraging better treatment of Mike's legacy and the future release of real outtakes that the fans and world want to hear.

0865479186|5.0|I was lucky enough to pick this up on a visit to England. I opened it on the flight home and was riveted for six hours.    First a caveat:  This is not the best-organized book I've ever read. American readers will have trouble following some of the regionalisms, both of language and of media coverage of health issues.  (As Goldacre points out, ridiculous media hysteria over \\"health scares\\" are almost always limited to a single nation.)  As an example, if you've never heard of the MMR debacle, I suggest you go to the index of the book and if that doesn't work, Google.  The book unfortunately references the problem several times before the primary discussion of it, and even then, I don't think Goldacre ever really defines what the controversy was, or even what \\"MMR\\" stands for.    That said, this book is so brilliant and so important, it gets five stars from me despite the flaws.  Also, even despite organizational problems, Goldacre has a readable and often quite dryly humorous writing style, which adds to the enjoyment.    \\"Bad Science\\" is an eye-opening introduction, written for the non-scientist, into the critical questions of what constitutes proof of cause and effect in the health sciences, what is required for valid research, and what to look for when you hear health claims.  He very clearly and easily leads the reader to understand such intimidating concepts as \\"reversion to the mean\\".  Do you think you know what a placebo is?  Well, okay, you know the basic concept, as I did when I started the book; but I was astonished and delighted at the breadth, depth, and importance of the placebo effect.    If read any health advice in the newspapers or magazines, or even watch the (comparatively competent) Dr. Oz on television, you will be astonished at how much of the advice is unproven, untrue, or possibly even dangerous.  If you have a sneaking suspicion about the claims of weight-loss products, and yet feel pulled in by those before and after pictures of fatties whohave become lean and trim (and usually tan, LOL) after taking the product, this book will teach you how to tell the valid claims from the invalid.    And don't think doctors necessarily know this stuff.

The older this young writer gets, the more convinced he seems to be of the need for length. You can also see how this band influenced alot of MJs mid 80s work.  However, there is a reason MJ never released this before; dont know what because I love it but probably because it didnt fit on the Bad album - it isnt 2010 and MJ always wanted to be a pioneer..one of the reasons why if you listen to 2001 Invincible Album it sounds as fresh as anything Rhianna, Black Eyed Peas, Alicia Keys or Jayz put out today.      So altogether; Michael is comforting for fans who just want to hear his voice on something they havent already heard a hundred times.  Its interesting for general music lovers just because MJ is an important pop artist in culture and if you are going to have an opinion you need to be familiar.  Some of the songs are cool enough to release anyway.  However, there is no point judging it nextto Thriller, Bad, Dangerous, Off the Wall, History, Invincilbe or even Blood on the Dance Floor because it isnt made by MJ..so it isnt an MJ album.  It is an ode to a much missed and loved artist by a money spinning Sony music, an ambitious Estate that want to cement MJs legacy, a handful of music industry talent who worked with MJ and want to contribute to that legacy.  So to conclude; if you listen to the album with this context in your head and dont try to compare it to an actual MJ album then it is a brilliant buy - great listen and will enhance your music collection.

B00432QAKK|4.0|This review will not focus on the merits of this classic TV show since anyone visiting this page already likes it enough to possibly buy the entire series on DVD.  Rather, this review will hopefully clear up the confusion regarding exactly what is being offered with this Complete Series collection.  Sony originally released the individual seasons on DVD from 2003 to 2009.  This 2010 Complete Series collection simply repackages the exact same DVDs from the individual seasons.  There are 32 discs in all spanning the entire 11 seasons for a total of 261 episodes.  Unfortunately, there is no episode list included showing what episodes are on each disc.  The bonus content is slim and includes:<br /><br />Season 1- 42 minute 2003 reunion special with all of the principal cast members.<br />Season 2- 13 hidden \\"Easter Eggs\\" featuring short interview clips with the cast.<br />Season 3- 10 hidden \\"Easter Eggs\\" of cast interview clips + the unaired \\"I'll See You in Court\\" episode.<br />Seasons 4 to 11- No series related extras.<br /><br />It should be noted that the opening theme has been replaced with generic music starting with season 3 due to music licensing issues.  Also, season 4 has 7 episodes that are the syndicated versions, meaning each is missing about a minute of footage from the original broadcast versions. All other seasons appear to have the original, uncut episodes.  The video is presented in its original full frame 1.33:1 aspect ratio and the audio is in 2.0 Dolby digital stereo.  Neither the picture nor sound quality shows any noticeable signs of remastering but are still generally good considering the age of the series.  The packaging is also worth mentioning as it is very different than the individual season sets.  The discs are housed inside a cardboard box measuring approximately 7.5\\"H x 5\\"W x 5.5\\"D.  Inside the box, there is a fold-out digi-pack with 9 clear plastic trays stacked on top of one other on either side, holding 2 overlapping discs per tray, with 4 trays holding 1 disc each.  Only time will tell just how well this case keeps its contents secure, but in terms of being a space-saver, this excels over other complete series DVD sets. So powerful is the result, the oil and gas industry, via a PR group, \\" Energy-In-Depth\\", drafted a paper circulating around the internet called \\"De-Bunking Gasland.\\" Fox responded with a 39 page retort,\\" Debunking the De-Bunkers\\". Commentators, bloggers and posters have been weighing in around the country whether they have seen the film or not. Viewers report reactions ranging from nightmares to insomnia to joining the fight.    Those of us living above the geologic layer known as the Marcellus shale have no need to ask why all the fuss. The 15 million or so who reside in or draw their drinking water from the watershed of the Delaware River, as well as residents of 34 other states living above gas bearing shale formations, perhaps ought to find out.    Synopsis: Youthful, sincere, witty, brilliant, urban hick Fox and his family receive an offer  to lease the old family hippie homestead located on a tributary of the Delaware in northeastern Pennsylvania for natural gas \\"exploration\\". Close to $100,000 for the right to drill a mile under their 19 acres in moist, luscious, secluded, fern and forest country. Fox has heard of the water well contamination from gas drilling in nearby Dimock, PA and embarks on a quest to discover the possible pitfalls to accepting the windfall. With remarkable ability to gain access into people's homes and lives, Fox makes friends everywhere he goes, documents people's horror stories, gets rebuffed by corporate gate keepers, dismissed by bureaucrats in charge of protecting the health and safety of we, the citizenry, and finds a couple of genuine scientific heroes along the way. He also discovers - surprise! - our evil former Vice President cleverly cleared the path for the expansion of a technique pioneered in environmentally deprived Texas, known as high pressure slick water hydraulic fracturing, which opened up previously unexploitable gas bearing shale formations to massive development in areas all over the country. One of which, the United States northeast's Marcellus shale, has been called the \\"Saudia Arabia of shales\\". Potentially the second largest resource of \\"natural\\" gas yet found in the the world.    In only his second effort at film directing, highly political theatre director Fox, along with a very skilled film editor, crafted a remarkably moving piece of work. Why do we allow corporations to roll over people's lives, trashing our various pursuits of happiness and right of quiet enjoyment of our real property? Why are representatives and bureaucrats so unresponsive and unemotional when presented with evidence of ill treatment of their constituents? Why do some brave souls risk their livelihood or at least their neighborhood standing in fighting for health and justice? These are among the questions that may haunt a viewer of \\"Gasland\\".    Is it possible not to be moved by 3rd generation cattle rancher, John Fenton, as he expounds, \\"This may not seem like much to most people, but its my way of life. My father and grandfather were the old time cowboys. This is my family's heritage, my wife's family's farm. We're proud of this. But by God, if your way of life is being besieged....I don't know what else you could do. I don't know where the hell I could go. This is happening everywhere. That's what I want people to know.\\" ? Is it possible not to understand the injustice, when seeing the Fenton family cabin perched on a dry Wyoming range country hillside, overlooking gas well pad, after pad, after pad; storage tank, after tank, after tank, or when seeing their home enveloped in a sick looking toxic fog, or watching tranquil mooers you may one day find on your dinner plate slurping from watering tanks amidst an industrial wasteland? Is it possible to see and hear all that, and, comprehending that the Fenton's do not own the gas rights to their ranch property - that all the mess was all imposed on them without their say and without benefit to them - and not be emotionally moved?    Maybe not if you make you living in or around the extraction of natural gas. Then you may be moved by \\"Gasland\\" in a different way; moved to near panic. What if people catch on that the current extraction process is a vast experiment, what if the public figures out that the risk, the potential trashing of our finite fresh water supply from a combination of toxins added in the fracturing process and naturally occurring elements and compounds released by the high pressure forcing of these fluids deep underground, is just too much of a gamble? What if people begin to think: we've got to get off hydrocarbons asap? Not worth the risk, not worth the environmental degradation and its potential effects on our loved ones health. Or on our ability to enjoy and renew ourselves in the natural world we ultimately depend upon for our existence.     These too are among the questions \\"Gasland\\" slips into a viewers mind. On screen, unintentionally, Fox proves himself one of the heros he brings into focus. His friendly, empathetic manner not only gains him amazing access, but wins viewers over. He is open minded, curious, funny, non judgmental when it comes to people ( not necessarily corporations), a bit disheveled, and very determined.     All of these characteristics are on display when you see him enter the modest home of Mike Markham and Marsha Medenhall in Weld County, Colorado. As Mike lights water directly from his tap on fire, Fox's first reaction is a completely unselfconscious: \\"Woah! Jesus Christ!\\". He joins Mike in a hard laugh at the absurd circumstance of a huge billow of flame erupting from the family kitchen faucet, then asks, as any adventurous kid might,\\"Can I do it?\\" When he does and is taken aback by the flames and the potential danger, he reels away from the tap physically moved. You see on his face a change from astonishment at his personal circumstance to true empathy, as he appears overcome by the emotion of the havoc that has entered the lives of his hosts. To the viewer it becomes clear, by the circumstance of having the camera turned on him, the heroic nature of the Director. It is hard not to think: those hippie parents sure did a good job with this one. Raised a real human being who feels sincerely for others, looks at societal issues critically and is able to act effectively to move things in a different direction, all with his sense of fun and passion for life intact.      If we are to move forward as a society in learning to treasure our home in the universe, we need real heroes like Josh Fox and John Fenton. And like Weston Wilson, long time EPA environmental engineer who boldly faces the camera and holds forth regarding citizen's experiencing well water contamination via migrating methane gas and plausibly, from \\"proprietary\\" chemical formulations used in hydraulic fracturing, \\"This is America. We shouldn't be assuming corporations can keep a secret. Especially when they are practicing in our backyard. The onus should be on the industry to prove that their practices are benign. Even if it weren't true, they are citizens of the United States and they certainly don't deserve to be exposed to secret chemicals. It's un-American.\\"    There is a myth going around the parts of Pennsylvania once know as the \\"Endless Mountains\\" and the \\"Pennsylvania Wilds\\". As residents find the rhythm and pace of the place where they chose to make their lives changing almost overnight, as semi-truck and pick up traffic become more like the overwhelming hassle they see in urban areas, as roads disintegrate before their eyes, as stories of incidents of pushy land men, water well contamination, illegal dumping and overweighttrucks become common place, as Texas license plates proliferate like rodents, the myth gains circulation: The shale area of Texas once looked like the present day northern tier of Pennsylvania. Then gas development began to take hold. As it grew, eventually the streams and rivers dried up from water withdrawls and associated micro and macro climatic changes in annual precipitation, leaving only bone dry stream beds most of the year. As more and more trees were removed from the forests to make room for well pads, storage tanks and ponds, pipelines, pipeyards, roads, metering and compressor stations, and all the other infrastructure of gas field development, remaining drought stressed trees began to die in droves. When the big trees were mostly all gone, succeeded mainly by invasive weed plant species, people moved off the land into endlessly growing urban and suburban centers which soon sprawled together in a huge toxic blob. Rural land was left abandoned, unfit for human and animal habitation, deemed an unnecessary obstacle to drilling and pipeline efficiency. The mountains were flattened, hollows filled in and result: Texas.    Will the myth prove prophetic for places you care about that are \\"on the shale\\"? Not if enough people join the fight. If you need motivation, check out Gasland.

0312600844|5.0|Books like Freedom are the reason I love to read. Most of the books I read are fast-moving thrillers, full of suspense, twists, and turns - the exact opposite of this book. The fact that it was chosen as an Oprah's Book Club selection prevented me from picking it up though. Nothing against her personally, I just assumed our tastes in literature wouldn't coincide. Fortunately for me I bought Freedom before Oprah selected it for her book club as well.     Walter and Patty Berglund are a typical Midwestern couple. They marry young and while Walter fell head-over-heals in love with Patty the moment he first laid eyes on her, Patty never felt that way about Walter. In her mind, she feels like she always settled for Walter. She loves the way he treats her more than she loves him. He's an environmental crusader, always looking after the little guy, which eventually leads him to the plight of American songbirds. She's a former high school and college athlete who was initially attracted to Walter's roommate but agrees to date Walter only after his roommate rejects her advances.    The brilliance of this book is Franzen's characters. He follows the Berglunds and their two children throughout their lives. He exposes their flaws and shortcomings as well as their humanity in a way that I can't remember reading in another book. I can't say that I considered any single character in the book \\"likable,\\" yet each one resonated with me, and ultimately I ended up caring about every one of them. My only qualification with recommending this book is its frequent adult content. Some will find that aspect of the book off-putting. But it would be shame if they put the book down because of it. The book as a whole is very rewarding and is sure to appear on every \\"Best of . . . \\" list for years to come.

B000063JZQ|4.0|This 1971 movie is simply a magnificent filming skill demonstration. Polansky takes a 400 years old drama, written in the most anti-cinematic language you can imagine, and he manages to generate a solid, powerful, dark film, which resists nicely to 2010 standards comparison. He also uses the filming industry resources at hand to make us believe we are in Middle Age Scotland, with its rainy skies, muddy roads, armored knights, stone castles and barbaric violence. No silly transposing to modern time, this IS what Shakespeare surely had in mind. Macbeth is a play of shocking bloodshed, and Polansky shows us all the blood scenes that happen off-stage in the original, thus adding a stunning realism. No matter how many miles of filmed violence are there since 1971, Duncan's murder here is still a terrifying thing to watch, believe me.<br /><br />Polansky players are very good. They are much younger than those we usually see on stage, because cinema requirements are different, so we can see true-to-story aged characters. Jon Finch is quite convincing, as all the rest of the male cast. Beautiful Francesca Annis lacks (completely) the dark, choked, evil voice Lady Macbeth needs (Kate Fleetwood in the recent Macbeth PBS presentation has that voice, wow!), and Annis \\"Hollywood look\\" may seem frivolous to some purists, but she is cleverly directed by Polansky, so finally makes it.<br /><br />I have no trouble with some non-original issues, like Ross unmoral collaboration with the tyrant and Donalbain visiting the witches: they distract, but don't spoil the whole picture. I think the film soundtrack, by The Third Ear Band, is quite poor: I miss a heavier, richer instrumentation on some scenes, according to the all-time masterpiece we're dealing with.<br /><br />My 1999 Columbia Pictures DVD has very good image remastering in HD, Dolby 2.0 sound, Spanish subtitles are just bare information (with some big mistakes). All in all, a highly recommended DVD.

031603438X|5.0|There is a mysterious aura to Keith Richards that draws people to him out of curiosity.  To me he always presented a contradicting persona, often pictured as sullen and aloof, yet feted as the consummate life of the party in rock and roll terms.  The disheveled and ragged appearance stereotypically conjures up the image of a junkie managing to survive from one fix to the next.  After all, the only survivors of a nuclear holocaust would be cockroaches ... and Keith Richards.  Yet the reality of the matter is that Keith Richards is all of the above and then some ... a recovering junkie that is also pure genius (not just musical), a survivor of the most hedonistic days of rock and roll, a family man and more importantly an openly honest man.  His book both explains and derails the mystery, providing a refreshingly deep and intimate portrait of an extremely interesting, talented and impressive individual.<br /><br />\\"Life\\" is more than a simple biography of a Rock and Roller ... it is, arguably, the only definitive history of the Rolling Stones from a somewhat objective point of view (after all, what does he have to gain or lose?).  \\"Keef\\", in all his rambling glory, spills his guts and gives us a fly on the wall perspective of his life beginning in war-torn Dartford all the way to what seems to be this very moment.  His life is also, of course, the life of the Rolling Stones.  The reader is taken for a journey that succinctly summarizes most every significant (or insignificant) event pertaining to the band.  The personnel changes, the studio sessions, the tours and the drugs.  Every step of the way, we are introduced to juicy tidbits of gossip, hilarious stories and personal feelings on just about everyone he knows and everything can remember.  There is even a testament or two that debunk decades-old myths about the man himself (like that infamous \\"blood transfusion\\" story).  But, the bulk of this memoir is dedicated to the soul or life-blood of Richard's existence ... music.  The overwhelming passion for music that courses through Richard's veins is evident on almost every page of this bulky 570 page monstrosity.  We see an unpretentious and amiable music icon as being just another giddy fan of his blues heroes; as well as someone willing to make music with anyone ... anywhere.<br /><br />Oddly enough, the book starts with Richards being involved in a random drug bust in the deep South (US) during the 1970s and the scenario reads like a scene from \\"Smokey and the Bandit\\" (cunning/brazen troublemaker Richards vs. intellectually challenged, local-yokel sheriff).  It's this classic back-against-the wall story told in Keith's classic sardonic tone that hooks the reader from the start and effectively generates the desire for Keith to start from the very beginning.  Although the book is basically one gigantic ramble, Richard's writing partner (James Fox) seems to have graciously crafted the story into a more readable format.  The numbered chapters are evenly spaced throughout and the intro to each chapter includes an italicized paragraph with tantalizing hints of each chapter's contents.  After reading the entire book, I sensed that these chapters hinted to three major phases in Keith Richard's life:  the meteoric rise of his early years (rise to superstardom to the sudden loss of innocence of Altamont that started a path to oblivion), the dark and blurred decade of the 1970s (where drugs and pure genius seem to function at such an amazingly productive level) and rebirth (a survivor seeing life with a relatively clear head).  Each chapter reads like Keith speaks and the stories are somewhat incoherent at times with brief, choppy sentences and a healthy peppering of Brit jargon (I'm still trying to figure out the apparent difference between \\"mate\\" and \\"friend\\").  But, as the chapters unfold, it becomes harder to dismiss Keith Richards as anything but intelligent, witty and charming.<br />Some pleasant surprises in \\"Life\\":<br /><br />1)The story of such an iconic Rock and Roll star in his own words is priceless.<br />2) The book can also be viewed as an ongoing guitar lesson ... Richard's opens up his bag of tricks and tells us how he crafted his historic musical contributions (like the discovery of the 5-string open-G).<br />3) The frank discussion of his addiction and the depravity he experience is somewhat shocking.<br />4) The open honesty and self-deprecating style of Richard's writing is refreshing, frequently humorous and appreciated.  His is simply a great storyteller.<br />5) He is definitely an odd character with a somewhat strange point-of-view (reaction to his son Tara's death).<br />6) The dichotomy he reveals between the real Keith Richards and the one we've seen and read about over the decades.<br /><br />I thought that almost 600 pages would be difficult to digest, until I realized that his story could legitimately be a multi-volume affair (think Churchill).  While I have nothing but praise for the book, I wished he would have written more on Brian Jones' death and Altamont, as well as more details on his relationship with Bill Wyman and Mick Taylor (who are scarcely mentioned in the book).  \\"Life\\" has given me a new perspective of Keith Richards ... he is definitely not the deep-fried burnout he appears to be.  He has transformed himself over the years to become this almost embarrassingly goofy senior citizen one can imagine mowing grass in plaid shorts, black knee-high socks and loafers ... but he also happens to have a whale of a story to tell.iconic Rock and Roll star in his own words is priceless.  2) The book can also be viewed as an ongoing guitar lesson ... Richard's opens up his bag of tricks and tells us how he crafted his historic musical contributions (like the discovery of the 5-string open-G).  3) The frank discussion of his addiction and the depravity he experience is somewhat shocking.  4) The open honesty and self-deprecating style of Richard's writing is refreshing, frequently humorous and appreciated.  His is simply a great storyteller.  5) He is definitely an odd character with a somewhat strange point-of-view (reaction to his son Tara's death).  6) The dichotomy he reveals between the real Keith Richards and the one we've seen and read about over the decades.    I thought that almost 600 pages would be difficult to digest, until I realized that his story could legitimately be a multi-volume affair (think Churchill).  While I have nothing but praise for the book, I wished he would have written more on Brian Jones' death and Altamont, as well as more details on his relationship with Bill Wyman and Mick Taylor (who are scarcely mentioned in the book).  \\"Life\\" has given me a new perspective of Keith Richards ... he is definitely not the deep-fried burnout he appears to be. B002ZG993Q|5.0|An excellent film. No, it is not fast-paced, yes, the camera does pan lovingly over the landscape (and takes some really outstanding aerial shots), yes, George says very little and there seems to be no traffic (of any kind) in this part of Italy. However, as a somber character study of a death dealer approaching death it is just excellent. I found the atmosphere, the pacing, the minimal dialogue (much of it in Italian) and the minutiae of 'Jack's' craft thoroughly absorbing. I see it as a counterpoint to the ridiculousness of the other films in the action/thriller genre - not that they aren't enjoyable on their own level. Whereas in other films a Matt Damon or a Pierce Brosnan would jump on a high powered motorcycle for the chase scene, Clooney uses a thoroughly Italian scooter. The weapons employed are small, subtle, appropriate. This film to me recalled Day of the Jackal (1973) in its ability to evoke the stealthy, paranoid world of the international assassin. Kudos to George for taking on such a quiet role and for bringing to it a depth of feeling (just watch his eyes) that really evokes the chilly world of unredeemed loneliness and isolation his chosen career necessitates. I like this film very much.

B0044KU7EQ|4.0|52 discs-all ranging between 50+ and 60+ minutes, with 1 disc (Vol. 38-Jimmy Rushing and Tampa Red) clocking in at 79 minutes+ and 1 disc (Vol. 25-Little Willie John and Smiley Lewis) in the 49+ minute range.  The sound (both mono and stereo) varies from artist to artist (and sometimes track to track) depending on the (vinyl) sources used.  Audiophiles will not be enamored with the sound in places, but blues lovers used to slightly inferior sound from old sources will find the music takes precedent over the sometimes rough sound.  I initially listened to this set through a good quality pair of headphones which puts everything front and center, and since it's not stated, I'm assuming this music has not been remastered in any way.  This isn't a case of the music fighting background hiss, like old Paramount recordings-these are just older analog sources used for the music.  Good quality tracks, for example, by Tommy Johnson or Skip James (Vol. 20), are harder to find, so background hiss, and snaps and crackles are inevitable.  There are also occasional short sonic anomalies on a few tracks throughout the set, but nothing that really gets in the way of enjoying some great blues.  The upside is that the music has a real warmth and straightforward honesty to it, which is sometimes absent from digital mastering.  Anyone familiar with the 10 CD box sets like \\"Diggin' Deeper\\", \\"Rhythm & Blues\\", or \\"Goin' Mad Blues\\" (released by the same company-with duplications here so beware) will have some idea of the sound.  But the chance to have so many fine early recordings in one, single collection, for blues lovers (like me), is to good to pass up.  For the most part, each disc has two performers, with artists like Bo Diddley, Jimmy Yancey, and Robert Johnson each having an entire disc to themselves.<br /><br />Each disc is in a fairly thick cardboard envelope with artist, song title, and song length on the back.  The outer box (approximately 10\\"x10\\") is substantial cardboard, with a lid that slips completely off.  The back of the box lists the performers, and has the (I'm assuming) caveat \\"Incl. Historical Recordings\\", which to me means the sound is less than pristine.  But I didn't purchase this set thinking the sound was perfect-older recordings are what they are-it's the music that's important here.  The photograph on the front of the box is carried over on all the CD sleeves.  The box is divided into fourths, with the discs stacked in three compartments.  The fourth contains the Hohner Puck harmonica, made in Germany, which is in it's own (1\\"x3\\") box-a nice touch.  There's also a 4 page advertising pamphlet on Hohner Harmonicas included.  The 27 page booklet (which is just slightly smaller than the outer box) contains some nice information (not always accurate) on the artists in alphabetical order.  There are a few (b&w) photographs of artists included with their write-ups.  However, it would have been nice (especially for blues newcomers-and easy for the record company) to have a photo of each artist next to their respective essay.  But for those interested, photographs are found easily enough both on the internet and in stand alone books on the blues.  A quick thought for newcomers-I recommend learning more about the blues, the era (s) and blues artists-it makes the music much more interesting and exciting.<br /><br />This is an overview of the blues, from the country to the city.  All the various styles of blues, featuring over 100 artists, are represented-acoustic country blues (Kokomo Arnold), New Orleans style (Huey \\"Piano\\" Smith), swamp blues (Arthur Gunter), big city electric blues (Buddy Guy), jump blues (Roy Milton), piano based blues (Jimmy Yancy), jazz/blues (Jimmy Rushing), religious (as opposed to true gospel) blues (Blind Willie Johnson), and some blues bordering on early r&b (Richard Berry-\\"Louie Louie\\").  Every style of blues has a number of representatives, from well known artists (Bobby \\"Blue\\" Bland, Bo Diddley, John Lee Hooker, Skip James, Elmore James, Little Walter, Magic Sam, Charley (Charlie) Patton, Bessie Smith, Jimmy Reed, Son House, Junior Wells, both Sonny Boy Williams 1&2, Robert Johnson, and so on), to a quite a few that may be new (Blue Lu Barker, Barbecue Bob, Cousin Joe, Tommy McClennan, Frankie Lee Sims, Peetie Wheatstraw (\\"the Devil's Son-in-Law\\"), Big Maceo, Big Maybelle, Robert Nighthawk, Eddie Taylor, as examples) to the casual listener.  To list all the artists would be quite a chore-so refer to the Amazon page, which lists the artists.  As often happens, songwriting credits are sometimes a bit loose, but the music is still great, no matter who claims credit.  The performances  are not arranged chronologically according to when they were recorded, so this is not a disc to disc history of the blues as such.  The artists are arranged more or less alphabetically, which makes for some aural jumps from style to style, but the music is so fine that that's a minor consideration.<br /><br />The music is from the early years (even the big city blues artists), with nothing contemporary, which helps with the focus of this set.  The country/acoustic blues are pure and straightforward, and the city/electric blues have some scorching performances.  The sheer time that could (and will) be spent listening to this set is truly staggering.  There is so much good music that demands to be heard that many people will find themselves going back for another listen to a favorite artist or possibly someone new to them.  This is a box set bordering on overwhelming in it's scope and size.  But the music is so good, so honest, so intense and  passionate, that it makes this collection a valuable addition to virtually anyone's blues library.<br /><br />Anyone who has a distinct bias towards the blues, no matter if you're a long time listener or are fairly new to the blues, will enjoy this collection.  There will be tracks that are familiar, but there will also be unfamiliar music here (unless you're a deep collector) that will help fill in a number of areas of blues styles.  This music has a deeper feel if you listen to it very late at night/very early in the morning when everything is quiet.  The warm, sometimes slightly distant, (vinyl) sound of these tracks gives this music real atmosphere-at times you feel as if you're listening to one of the old radio stations that plays classic old blues records, which you've somehow stumbled across and picked up late at night-and that late night sound and feel gives this music even more magic.e Hooker, Skip James, Elmore James, Little Walter, Magic Sam, Charley (Charlie) Patton, Bessie Smith, Jimmy Reed, Son House, Junior Wells, both Sonny Boy Williams 1&2, Robert Johnson, and so on), to a quite a few that may be new (Blue Lu Barker, Barbecue Bob, Cousin Joe, Tommy McClennan, Frankie Lee Sims, Peetie Wheatstraw (\\"the Devil's Son-in-Law\\"), Big Maceo, Big Maybelle, Robert Nighthawk, Eddie Taylor, as examples) to the casual listener. 0316098337|4.0|In her seventh novel \\"Room\\", Irish born writer (and now Canadian citizen) Emma Donoghue has created a must read for all. Triggered by the 2008 Josef Fritzel Case, this horrific yet touching novel, now shortlisted for the Man Booker prize, explores the everlasting bond of love between a mother and her son.  Seven years ago a young woman, kidnapped at nineteen, was locked in a fortified room and repeatedly raped. She now has a five year old son, \\"Jack\\", and it is through his thoughts that Donoghue tells their emotional journey of survival and escape.   Its publisher claims it to be \\"a novel like no other\\". I hasten to agree with this statement as Donoghue's unique use of language appears to explore the mind of a child with deep and meaningful understanding. The language was so detailed that I instantly found myself desperately trying to remember my thoughts as a child in comparison to Jack's.   Jack's entire life has been lived in a solitary room that measures just eleven foot square; to him, Room is the entire world. The author is able to reflect Jack's youth and innocence by creating characters out of inanimate objects within the room, and giving them a name and gender. Readers will begin to feel an emotional bond towards characters such as \\"Wardrobe\\", \\"Rug\\" and \\"Plant\\" who make up a significant part of Jack's world. As a consequence, the room takes on a life of its own.    Donoghue makes no attempt to hide disturbing events which occur throughout Jack and Ma's emotive journey. When Ma's kidnapper \\"Old Nick\\" comes into the room at night, Jack is forced to hide in Wardrobe and listen to the creaks of the bed. Using a child's innocent account to describe such a horrific event makes this an unbearable world for the reader as well as for Jack and Ma.    Although the narrative is told from Jack's viewpoint, we learn much about Ma. To Jack, Room is the only world which exists, but for Ma, it is a dismaying prison in which she has tried to build a normal life for her son.I eventually found myself empathising with the Ma through Jack's narrative. It's clear that she has spent the last five years nurturing and teaching Jack, but she chooses to let him believe that there is no world outside Room. Ma is a survivor. Despite the years of confinement, her determination and love for Jack encourages her to continue dreaming up ways to escape.  After their dreams of escaping Room become reality, Jack and Ma are the centre of a media storm. Both Jack and Ma struggle to cope in \\"Outside\\" and for the first time we see their relationship become vulnerable.  Although the storyline is endearing, I don't believe that this book would have been so successful if it had not been narrated through Jack's thoughts. Donoghue's ingenious use of language and gripping storyline create a substantial amount of sympathy for Ma and Jack, but also evoke a distinctive feeling of gratitude within the reader, which lingers on for days. I felt that I could no longer perceive the world in the same way; the novel provided me with an overwhelming sense of thankfulness for the privileged life I lead. For me, \\"Room\\" highlights a vivid and beautiful expression of maternal love between a mother and her son.   This book will touch your heart.

B0009F9O6M|3.0|As to be expected, the band third studio set \\"H To He Who am the Only One\\" was recorded amidst another round of personnel turmoil.  This time around former The Misunderstood bassist Nic Potter decided to tender his notice midway through the recording sessions.  King Crimson guitarist Robert Fripp was brought in as a guest and the shake up didn't seem to have a major impact on the recording sessions.  Produced by John Anthony, this may have been the band's creative zenith.  Mind you, as you probably figured out from the goofy title (anyone got a clue?), it wasn't their most commercial, or accessible ousting so newbies and the casual fan might want to sample something else in the VDGG catalog before jumping in with this one.    - Even though it stretched out over eight minutes and found David Jackson literally freaking out on sax, 'Killer' stood as a fantastic song and one of those progressive pieces that deserved it's classic status.  Propelled by a surprisingly commercial riff and Peter Hammill's dark and scary vocals, the plotline was largely lost on me (using a shark's life as an allegory for life as an anti-social introvert?), though I have to admit that the 'fish can't fly' chorus has always made me smile.  - 'House with No Door' stood as the song for folks who didn't think VDGG could put together a straightforward commercial track.  A simply stunning ballad, Hammill kept his over-the-top tendencies in check, turning in a stark and compelling performance highlighted by what may have been Jackson's prettiest flute solo.  Great piano and organ from High Banton and Hammill.    My only complaint - they faded it out too soon.  - A two part suite, 'The Emperor In His War - Room' featured Robert Fripp, though his performance was relatively low keyed and didn't kick in under towards the start of 'The Room'.  Musically 'The Emperor' segment was a fairly conventional ballad apparently meant to provide insight into the mindset of a political tyrant ...  you can see why I normally don't try to second guess lyrics.  Not quite as commercial 'House with No Door', but with a pretty and distinctive melody.  'The Room' opened up with Fripp, then bounced around between slower and more upbeat segments.  Given the track's complexity, Guy Evans turned in some nice drumming to keep it tied together and focused.  - Longtime fans seem to consider 'Lost' the standout performance, but I'm going to go against the current and suggest that clocking in at over 11 minutes the two part suite was one of the lesser performances.  To my ears it captured Hammill and company at their most theatric and over-the-top pompous. Musically it was all over the place giving all the players an opportunity to stretch out.  Certainly listenable and occasionally even pleasant, but not my favorite.  - Hum, imagine VDGG doing science fiction lyrics ... well you don't need to go any further than the closer 'Pioneers Over C'.  Musically this one didn't do a great deal for me, the band bouncing around an extended piece without any real form or format.  On the other hand it had a fascinating lyric that seemed to have something to do with the possibilities of time travel (I/m not a big sci-fi fans).  I borrowed this Hammill interview off the official VDGG website:    \\"This is my only attempt at writing a specifically sci-fi song, although the balancing is much more towards fiction than science.  Man's first plunge into the unknown territory beyond the speed of light (c): in the light of the discoveries necessary for the attempt, the date is meaningless, although in rational terms it is ludicrously optimistic. The Pioneers... the first hypernauts... are, because of theoretical deficiencies, thrown into time-warp or absolute relativity, in which they exist as 'creatures' of limitless imagination but total non-physicality. They are thus potentially ghouls, ghosties, poltergeists and all manner of indefinable Forces: this is one possible explanation but, truly, in such circumstancesexplanations are meaningless, irrelevant and totally speculative.  My only regret is that I found it necessary to provide a certain chronological continuity in order to remain, if faintly, within the bounds of comprehension. I don't pretend that there are any answers here, and any questions are entirely subjective.\\"    Summation - One of the lost treasures in the VDGG catalog and something every progressive fan should at least hear, if not own.    \\"H To He Who am the Only One\\" track listing:  (side 1)  1.) Killer   (Peter Hammil - Hugh Banton - Chris Judge-Smith) -   2.) House with No Door   (Peter Hammill - David Jackson) -   3.) The Emperor In His War - Room       i.) The Emperor    (Peter Hammill)       ii.) The Room   (Peter Hammill)     (side 2)  1.) Lost        i.) Dance In Sand and Sea   (Peter Hammill)        ii.) Dane In Frost   (Peter Hammill)   2.) I read Gary Taubes's \\"Why We Get Fat\\" with interest and initially I was convinced by his conclusions drawn from research and world-wide body type comparisons. Not to keep you in suspense; the answer to why we are fat is that we eat carbohydrates. Fat does not make you fat. Exercise does not make you thin. Fatty meats, or any meat or eggs, do not make you fat. It's the pasta, potatoes, and all other fiber-rich vegetables and fruits that make you fat.<br />[This book was written before news of the two-week all potato diet came out in which the man lost 20 pounds. B000WS4P5G|5.0|Though grand assertions of personal malevolence are hardly rare in the metal world, few approach the declaration in a manner quite like Glenn Danzig does here. With his third major band's debut, Glenn's punk roots have disappeared almost entirely, replaced by a sparse, blues metal sound that places Danzig's remarkably forceful vocals front and center. Though the punk world is not known for producing first-rate vocalists, Danzig's marvelous work here places him on the list of the great hard rock/metal singers. Danzig's effort here rather reminds of a more gruff version of the other pseudonymous metal legend whose name begins with D, the sadly departed Ronnie James Dio. While the instrumental aspects of each band are very different, the singers share a similar appeal--both are extraordinarily expressive and fill the potentially ludicrous music with genuine passion. All the credit, however, does not belong to the vocals alone, and the sinisterly minimalist instrumental attack matches provides a fitting base for Danzig's theatrical musings.<br /><br />For many listeners, myself included, \\"Danzig\\" may not make that strong of an impact upon first listen. Few widely released albums have a more basic, demo-like production/sound: J. Christ's lone guitar has a plain, not terribly heavy distortion and the rhythm section is strictly utilitarian. Initially it all sounds a bit the same, but soon the vocal hooks ingratiate themselves and the instrumental subtleties are revealed, all while a uniform and quite effective atmosphere is maintained. Though everything here qualifies as a kind of atmospheric blues metal, Danzig and company ring a few twists from the formula, as in \\"Am I Demon,\\" which brings a slightly punkish energy to the album, the somewhat gothic \\"End of Time,\\" which predicts some of their later work, and \\"She Rides,\\" which has a kind of lithe sleaziness distinct from the other tracks. (\\"She Rides\\" is apparently a stripper favorite, which comes as no surprise.) The album as a whole, however, is dominated by midpaced, catchy rockers like \\"Twist of Cain,\\" \\"Mother,\\" and the Zeppelin-esque closer \\"Evil Thing,\\" all of which have a quality vocal hook and powerful main riff containing the best of Christ's back-to-basics style. The production also hides a few details that add immensely to the album, such as the barely audible backing/harmony vocals that pop up sporadically, the female choir that emerges in a few choruses and even a little bit of horn in \\"Soul on Fire.\\" (One of the best tracks, by the way.) The album does lose a little momentum as it progresses, with weakest tracks \\"Possession\\" and \\"The Hunter\\" coming in the second half, but it never truly bogs down and has no definite filler.<br /><br />It is, perhaps, best that there aren't too many other albums out there quite like \\"Danzig.\\" Even the rather similar \\"Danzig II\\" has a richer, somewhat more dynamic sound. But, as a one shot deal, the kind of hyper-minimalism displayed here is quite effective. But, as a one shot deal, the kind of hyper-minimalism displayed here is quite effective. Check it out.
